  219. The Shea Butter itself is great! It's a wonderful, long lasting moisturizer, and has a nice nutty (almost chocolatey) scent. I put it on my hands this morning, and my hands have not dried out, even through a few hand washes. It is a little difficult to remove from the container, but I discovered that a slightly warm spoon works very well for scooping it out.<br /><br />Now, the reason for only 3 stars: the e-book. Those of you who did not receive it, don't worry, you're not missing much. As I started reading it, I noticed a few typo's (using the wrong &#34;to&#34;, &#34;where&#34; vs. &#34;wear&#34;, etc). Not a big deal, lots of ebooks have typo's. I also noticed some of the pages are out of order...not cool. The major issue, however, is content. It does have some good information about shea butter itself, but I cannot trust any of the recipes in it. Maybe I'm a little under-qualified to be writing this, because I have never actually made soap, but I have done lots of research on the soapmaking process, and plan to make soap in the near future. The most obvious problem with the soap recipes in this book is the fact that several of them do not include lye as an ingredient. If you do not use lye, you will not get soap, period. The non-lye recipes might give you a nice lotion bar, but they will certainly not be soap. The next issue with the soap recipes (that do include lye...I can't speak for lotion bars) is that the instructions say to put the soap in the refrigerator to cool after pouring it into the mold. While milk soaps generally are cooled, because the sugar in the milk combined with lye produces a lot of heat, I have never come across a soapmaking resource that suggests cooling a non milk soap. In fact, most soapmakers actually insulate their soap to keep it warm through the saponification process. I don't know what refrigeration would do to the soap, but it certainly won't help anything. My last problem with the soap recipes is that they also say to wrap the bars in wax paper and store in an airtight container. This is probably a good way to store lotion bars, but soap needs ventilation. Air circulation helps soap to cure and dry out. Wrapping it in wax paper seems unwise.<br /><br />I can't speak for the other recipes, but unfortunately, since the soap recipes are so far from reliable, I would not trust any of the other recipes in this book. If you want to make stuff out of shea butter, I suggest doing some research before attempting any of the recipes in this book.<br /><br />One final thing I wanted to point out is the book does discuss the difference between ivory and yellow shea butter. They are basically the same, and I am perfectly content with my ivory shea buttter, but what if I wanted yellow? The sticker on the lid of my shea butter has boxes labeled &#34;ivory&#34; and &#34;yellow&#34;, with ivory being marked. It's a minor issue, but there is no way to specify during ordering which version you want. It seems to be just the luck of the draw which color you get. I noticed while browsing other shea butters on Amazon, that a lot of them do have an option for choosing ivory or yellow. Having a choice would be nice..e bars in wax paper and store in an airtight container. This is probably a good way to store lotion bars, but soap needs ventilation. Air circulation helps soap to cure and dry out. Wrapping it in wax paper seems unwise. I can't speak for the other recipes, but unfortunately, since the soap recipes are so far from reliable, I would not trust any of the other recipes in this book. If you want to make stuff out of shea butter, I suggest doing some research before attempting any of the recipes in this book. One final thing I wanted to point out is the book does discuss the difference between ivory and yellow shea butter. They are basically the same, and I am perfectly content with my ivory shea buttter, but what if I wanted yellow? The sticker on the lid of my shea butter has boxes labeled &#34;ivory&#34; and &#34;yellow&#34;, with ivory being marked. It's a minor issue, but there is no way to specify during ordering which version you want. It seems to be just the luck of the draw which color you get. I noticed while browsing other shea butters on Amazon, that a lot of them do have an option for choosing ivory or yellow. Having a choice would be nice..
